<h2>All Reviews</h2>

<ol>
    <li> I have owned this sleep mask for a few years now. Initially, I only used it on the rare occasion that I had bad migraine, which for me, can cause severe sensitivity to light. I also use it whenever traveling as you never quite know how much light will shine through your hotel window. Most recently, I&#x27;ve tried to use it on nights that I wake up a lot. I must be a light sleeper and having the mask on my face just seems to help me stay asleep or go back to sleep quickly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;- It&#x27;s stays on your face/head! I pull my hair in a ponytail and then wrap this around my face, securing with the velcro attached at the ends. You can adjust how you need to, but as long as it&#x27;s reasonably secure, it doesn&#x27;t slide off, which is a problem I&#x27;ve had with skimpier face masks with the skinny elastic band.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- This is a quality product. It&#x27;s well made and seems very durable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The fabric fully covers your under eye area because of the cut above the nose on the mask. So it really does fit snuggly against your face and block out any light.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons - I&#x27;ve only recently discovered this during a Texas spring where humidity runs high. I wake up kind of hot in this mask now that it&#x27;s warming up outside, even if we have the a/c on. Maybe this company makes the same mask with a cooler fabric for warm months. I&#x27;m not sure...have not checked. I still use it and just remove it if I get too hot. But if you&#x27;re using this regularly and need it for something like daytime sleeping, you might consider this.</li>
    <li> Best sleep I&#x27;ve had in a while</li>
    <li> This was one of the worst sleep masks I&#x27;ve ever had.  It goes over your ears but the fabric that is inside as the filler, is LOUD.  It crinkles all night, I mean ALL NIGHT... it does block out the sun, and is comfortable, but it constantly woke me up with the crinkling over my ears.  I&#x27;ve thought of maybe sewing some flannel fabric on the inside to decrease the sound, maybe I&#x27;ll do that when I pick up sewing :P haha</li>
    <li> They are fantastic, however they need to be a little longer in back.</li>

    <li> I use it every night, i use it every time i nap. This has made my sleep better and makes me fall asleep faster. It&#x27;s high quality and can withstand my night tumblings. I love this mask and recommend everyone who wants a good mask get this!</li>

The mask is very effective in blocking out light but even with the earplugs, it didn&#x27;t block out all of the sound. In fact, I heard vague sounds from without and less vague noise from my own breathing and the blood beating on my eardrum. Still, it made it easier for me to sleep under somewhat adverse conditions.</li>

The Sleep Master was by far the most comfortable fit for me compared to the [[ASIN:B0027OUUFW Tempur-Pedic Sleep Mask]] and the [[ASIN:B000M3HEMC Mindfold Black out Sleeping Mask]] as long as I planned to keep my eyes closed.    My goal for a sleep mask is to assist in catching 1-2 more hours of good sleep in the summer months when early morning light starts streaming in about 5 AM through a window in my bedroom that is nearly impossible to adequately drape without undo financial expense.  Otherwise I am a relatively easy sleeper.  I don&#x27;t expect to wear the mask through the whole night -- just slip it on if I am sleeping lightly or not at all in those final hours.  I am most interested if work-related issues cut my available sleep options down to only 4-5 hours and these are further hampered by summer light.  Thus my experience may be different than those who routinely need a full 8-hour mask.    I think that one of the most difficult issues in sleep masks is that having differently shaped faces is going to influence whether we are personlaly satisfied or disappointed -- particularly if the expectation is a total blackout of external light.  Its hard to get something to fit well enough without being uncomfortable and intruding on sleep while still providing extreme \\&quot;black out\\&quot;.  Also, the longer we are exposed to low light, the more sensitive we will beocme to just a few stray photons.    That said. This mask excelled for comfort as long as my eyes were closed.  It was optimized for sleep and relies on closed eyes somewhat to minimize awareness of external light.  It might shift a little with sidelying or leaning against an airline window but not markedly enough for me to interfere with nasal breathing or create sinus pressure.  It might allow more light leakage after moving around some during sleep (particularly at the bottom and around the nose, but so far this has not been a major concern to me.      If I planned to use it for meditation, I would need to adjust my expectations some -- it doesn&#x27;t accomodate eyes open as well ss the Mindfold or Tempur-Pedic.  However, its lighter weight and silkier feel against the skin are an advantage if one meditates with eyes closed. Thus willingness to make some adaptations might make it a favorite.   For persons who wear a mask for other purposes, such as simulated experiences of visual impairment, for holotropic breathwork sessions, or a migraine phase with photosensitivity in which complete blackout might not be unnecessary, I think this model could work very nicely.      SUMMARY    What I liked best about the Sleep Master was a fairly moderate price, excellent comfort, and quite decent light blockage. Ordinarily I would also like the sound dampening feature of the retaining strap.  This would likely be a plus for many other users.  (But it becomes a bit of a hinderance for me on call nights, because I do want to hear my phone well...so on these nights I wear the Tempur-Pedic.) If 1/2 star rankings were permitted I would rank it as 4 and 1/2.  I didn&#x27;t rate it as a five-star product because I still wish that it was possible to have my eyes open without scrapping my eyelids, and a bit more light blockage.       Unfortunately, none of the masks I tried were completely satisfying for comfort and blackout, despite being on the moderate to higher end of the price range for this type of product.  I suspect it is inevitable that no single mask will optimally fit both men and women across all levels of fitness and facial contours.  Making more customer-specific masks may be possible, but these could then be harder to sell by mail when understandably there is a no-return-if-used policy due to hygeine policies.</li>

The company should really make the following changes: slim down the back of the mask so it has less fabric and less thick Velcro / is softer; find a slightly lighter fabric which is more durable and does not start to pill after slight friction (i.e. if I accidentally rub the mask against the exposed brick wall near my bed), add some form of rigid structure to the nose bridge, perhaps add some form so there is less friction with your eye lids, consider adding some concave form to the area of fabric that overlaps with your check bone - this would help keep out a lot more light, if I try going to sleep when someone else in the room needs all the lights on - I still notice light leaking in from the cheek area - just enough to bug me and keep me from falling asleep fast.     <li> First of all, the effect of this product on my sleeping was instant and amazing.  I have never used a sleep mask before, so I was a little apprehensive about wearing one, particularly after reading some of the criticisms below.  I tried the mask for an afternoon nap the day I got it.  It felt mildly odd when I put it on for the first time, but it was very soft, comfortable, and adjustable, so I got used to it almost immediately.  I had a great sleep that afternoon and have slept beautifully ever since. (Not the case before I started using the mask.)      The mask really blocks out the light and the padding muffles sound well, but not completely.  That&#x27;s actually a plus to me, because it blocks out just enough sound to remove distractions, but no so much that I can&#x27;t hear my husband, the alarm clock, etc.  I suspect that if you used the earplugs that come with, you could really block out almost all sounds, if that&#x27;s your goal.      It&#x27;s also easy to slide the mask up and on your forehead and back down onto your face; you don&#x27;t have to completely remove it or re-Velcro it to temporarily look or move around during the night.    Now, to the downsides.  Because of the padding, the mask can get a little warm over the course of the night.  However, in spite of being warm-natured and living in a warm climate (Texas), I don&#x27;t find it at all uncomfortable.  I don&#x27;t even notice that it IS warm until I take it off--and suddenly my face feels cooler.  So I&#x27;d agree with those reviewers who remarked on this point, but unless you are really, really warm-natured, this shouldn&#x27;t be a dealbreaker.    Also, I did notice some of the black rubbing off on the pillowcases.  However, the black washed out completely and the problem also seemed to diminish after the first washing of the mask.  (I cautiously hand washed the mask in Woolite and let it air dry and that seemed to work well.)  I&#x27;m guessing this is a problem of fibers rubbing off while the mask is new, but even if it&#x27;s not, the improvement in sleep is well worth this minor inconvenience.    In short, if you&#x27;re hesitating buying this product because of the problems noted in some of the other reviews, in my opinion the plusses far, far outweigh the minuses.</li>

    <li> \\&quot;Excellent. Item as described. Easy to use. Stays in place. Also, partially blocks out sound for good nights sleep. Arrived on time. Would use this company again. Thanks.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The above is the sincere but \\&quot;knee jerk\\&quot; review I dashed out when contacted by Sleep Master. It is an incomplete review as I did not want to take more time. However, after posting, I had a chance to read what others were saying about this product -  and about their criteria for a good sleep. The two biggest complaints were 1) eye areas not contoured enough and therefore interferes with REM sleep (eye movements during sleep) and 2) that this mask did not block sound very well. Like many of you, I am sensitive to light and noise and have tried many different sleep masks through the years (the worst being the cheap masks you get from airlines when on a long distance flight).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The fact is that no single product can provide protection for REM sleep and block 100% of the light and noise. Therefore, I use the &#x27;Sleep Master&#x27; in combination with two other products. I first put on a contoured sleep mask to achieve protection for REM sleep. I use the &#x27;[[ASIN:B000CCI4YU Dream Essentials Sweet Dreams Contoured Sleep Mask]]&#x27; but use whatever works best for you. I then put in place my ear plugs. I use the the &#x27;[[ASIN:B000R8Y1Y6 Hearos Ultimate Softness Series Ear Plugs]]&#x27; but again use any plugs that you prefer. Lastly, I wrap the &#x27;Sleep Master Mask&#x27; around (over top of) the contoured mask and ear plugs. The &#x27;Sleep Master&#x27; is great as the outer layer as it is smooth and flat. This is important to me as I turn from side to side when sleeping and tend to loose or dislodge most masks and ear plugs. Because the &#x27;Sleep Master&#x27; fits over the fairly rigid &#x27;Sweet Dreams Contoured Mask&#x27;, I can pull it tight enough to stay securely put while not placing pressure directly upon my eyes and adversely effecting REM sleep. It also keeps me from losing my ear plugs. The &#x27;Sleep Master&#x27; provides me an &#x27;additional&#x27; layer for blocking both light and sound. This may sound cumbersome but once in place it is the most comfortable and effective solution I have found. Does this solution block 100% of light and sound. No. But then again nothing will. Occasionally, a very small speck of light may get through and sound is still barely detectable but very muted and seems far away (for those of you extremely light sleepers you may want to add a white noise machine to the mix). The bottom line is use what ever &#x27;combination&#x27; works for you. For now, the &#x27;Sleep Master&#x27; is the perfect and indispensable outer layer to my own solution and I recommend it highly. A comment to Sleep Master - If you could incorporate a more rigid contour mask into the inner layer of the Sleep Master Mask then this layered approach might be unnecessary.</li>

The large, enveloping size makes it effective at blocking out light, and, at least for me, much less likely to slide off or, say have a strap get caught in an uncomfortable position behind my ear (there are no straps with this one).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only caveat is that I don&#x27;t think anyone should buy this for noise suppression.     <li> This mask has a very silky feel, is padded and very comfortable. Its large size works very well in keeping out light. The Velcro closure in the back works so much better than the type with elastic bands. I am so pleased with this sleep mask that I ordered one to give as a gift.</li>
    <li> NOTE:  I am changing my review from 2 stars to 4.  I know, I&#x27;m surprised myself, too.  My original review is below, but I&#x27;ve found over time that I&#x27;ve grown to like this mask.  Specifically, I love the soft silkiness of the fabric, and I&#x27;ve settled on a not-too-tight but not-too-loose way of closing the velcro such that it doesn&#x27;t push in on my eyes too much, yet still stays mostly in place, with just a bit of light coming through around the nose area.  I still find it to be not possible to sleep on my back using this mask, so I&#x27;ve made a point to only sleep on my side when I wear it.  This has not been as big of an issues as it at first seemed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;---&lt;br /&gt;This is a decent sleep mask, with some major flaws, and some serious over-hype.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;- the material feels very nice&lt;br /&gt;- it is thicker, and does a decent job blocking out light if worn tightly (though see below)&lt;br /&gt;- it has velcro in the back, so you can adjust the tightness&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;- If you&#x27;re a back sleeper, forget it - the velcro is so thick that it will feel bumpy on the back of your head;  I&#x27;ve tried positioning the closure up higher on my head as well as lower, and it&#x27;s just not comfortable&lt;br /&gt;- The ear coverage does absolutely nothing for dampening sound - that&#x27;s just marketing gibberish (which would still leave this a fine mask, if it weren&#x27;t for the other issues)&lt;br /&gt;- I found that in order to get the mask on tightly enough to fully block out light around my nose area I had to tighten the velcro to be quite snug.  The problem with that is that the velcro itself is positioned exactly in the area where your eyes are.  What that means is that in order to tighten the mask, the most pressure is applied directly to your eyes.  I think this issues could be alleviated if they had two strips of velcro, one above and one below, so that the main tightening could be on other - less delicate - areas of the face.  For me, if I tighten the mask enough to block out light, myeyes feel the pressure and my vision is blurry and uncomfortable by morning.  Not good!&lt;br /&gt;- The price just isn&#x27;t justified - I had just as much eye coverage with none of the back-of-the-head velcro issues with masks less than half the price</li>

    <li> 3/5 stars. Above average.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The top rated review here on amazon seems extremely defensive of this sleep mask and a bit cynical and patronizing towards people who this sleep mask clearly doesn&#x27;t work for, a little odd and rude of them to be. The truth of the matter is is that a sleep mask is a very personal choice and depends on the shape of a persons head/nose and what may work for one may not work for another. In the same way a body soap may work for someone but that may also irritate another persons skin, it&#x27;s a personal thing. In my review here I&#x27;ve tried to look at this from not just how it works for me but how it works for the broader spectrum of people. Please don&#x27;t listen to reviews that slam people whose reviews differ from them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am one who needs pitch black to sleep and as it has been shown it is much healthier to sleep in complete darkness a functional and comfortable sleep mask is ideal. Especially when rays of sunlight come through in the early morning.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I came to amazon knowing they would have a wide selection and this one seemed to be the holy grail of sleep masks yet the reviews seem divided so I will try to hit on the important points.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. The mask is very wide which is important to block light out. However the nose slot may or may not fit someones nose. The photo showing the sleep mask on the woman fits her so perfectly in every way (nose, forehead, head size) it would be nice if everyone&#x27;s face was so perfectly proportioned but that is not the case. For me this doesn&#x27;t block out all the light but does block most and I haven&#x27;t found one that blocks all light. Depending on how this fits your nose/forehead it may block out more or less light.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. The mask does not have an elastic but instead wraps around and overlaps and Velcros. It is wide all the way around and barely narrows at all (it does not narrow nearly as much as the second two photos seem to show), it is also padded all the way around. This makes for a very thick band at the back of your head. If you sleep on your back, like I do this may bother you. Even if you push the back of it down toward your neck it is still in the way. However it is very gentle against your head and unlike many elastic ones it does not hurt the top of your ears, it is also easier to adjust than most elastic ones. If you have a very very large head this may not fit you or wrap all the way around. I have a medium sized head and it fits me fine (and has about 6 inches of excess).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. The sleep mask is basically firm but gentle foam covered in satin. The foam is gentle against my eyes but I don&#x27;t wrap it too tight (read on as to why this might be a problem). It is very soft and I have not had any problems with it bleeding in the laundry or on my pillow. I wash it on gentle cycle (in a lingerie bag) in cooler water and hang it to dry. You could hand wash it if you wanted but whatever you do don&#x27;t put it in the dryer. The velcro has held up and the mask is durable and well made.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. I sleep in a cool environment and live in a generally non-humid climate and prefer to bundle up in blankets in the winter than crank the heat up. I also don&#x27;t sweat easily and really need to be working out. I sleep with my head exposed but this sleep mask makes me sweat. Which really surprised me. Satin isn&#x27;t breathable AT ALL. The sleep mask isn&#x27;t breathable and is so wide covering so much of your face that it makes me sweat and I assume this may happen to others. I wish it was made out of some more breathable but the satin is very soft (read on).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5. The satin is very slippery and as it is so wide all the way around and never narrows to hug your head the sleep masks moves everywhere when I sleep. I toss and turn in my sleep (which some people stay still) and the satin just slips and moves all over my head with nothing to prevent it. I have woken up with the back of it over my eyes or with it completely off my head on my pillow. If you try to tighten it enough to keep it from moving it will put pressure on your eyes which you may wake up with a headache and your eyes very irritated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6. The cost. The item is well made and not cheap or going to fall apart. It also isn&#x27;t made in China but in the US. It will last a lifetime and washes up nicely. If the sleep mask works for you then it is worth the price for a goodnight sleep. If it doesn&#x27;t then it is a waste of $25 but amazon is very good with returns. I recommend you wear it every day for at least three weeks before judging it to allow yourself to get used to it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On a side note this doesn&#x27;t block sound. That is just silly. It&#x27;s a sleep mask, invest in quality earplugs (try Hearos).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall if you have a very very large head or differently shaped nose this may not work for you. If you sweat easily or sleep in a hot/humid environment this may not work for you. If you move around or toss and turn in your sleep this may not work for you. In the end it just comes down to what works for you. If you have tried other sleep masks and they are not working out then this may definitely be worth at least a try. If you have never had/worn a sleep mask before and are just starting out I would recommend you first try the basic banana shaped sleep mask and go from there. 3/5 stars. Definitely not a universal sleep mask.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would like to do a slight update. I was recently reading FAQs and other information on the companies own site and I have to clear up a few things for those who are reading that as well. If you buy this mask please do not replace it once a year, the company just wants your money and there is no reason to do that as it does not wear out like that. This item does not solve bed head in any way or \\&quot;keep a ladies hair in place\\&quot;, due to the rubbing from the back of the mask your hair will probably look worse in the morning than it would without the mask. Lastly, but very importantly (please read) this mask does NOT reduce noise. In reading their website I am shocked at how much they put forward the noise reduction to the extent that they say it might be a safety concern that you can barely hear! This is laughable! Cloth covering part of your ear is not going to reduce noise at all. They even say \\&quot;If you choose to use these ear plugs with Sleep Master, please be careful because you will not hear anything\\&quot;. This may be true but it would be entirely because of your choice of earplugs NOT the sleep mask. They also say wonderful things about the complementary ear plugs provided, the ear plugs provided are not great. As I mentioned earlier if you are looking for total sound blockage try Hearos.llow. If you try to tighten it enough to keep it from moving it will put pressure on your eyes which you may wake up with a headache and your eyes very irritated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6. The cost.     <li> I was expecting something great for my $25 sleep mask. Boy was I mistaken. I hate to give a laundry list of issues, but with this item, I can&#x27;t help but do just that. So, here goes:&lt;br /&gt;1) This mask doe *NOT* block out light. I repeat...it is *NOT* opaque! Lying in bed with the mask on, face towards the bed lamp on the other side of the bed, open my eyes, there is a distinct blue glow. And the bed lamp isn&#x27;t very bright! So no. This mask will not give you cave darkness. Unlike every other mask I have ever used, this one does *NOT* block light&lt;br /&gt;2) The stitching of the mask where it goes over the bridge of the nose is rough and irritating. If worn in a manner that is deemed comfortable, the stitching will rub against the bridge of your nose.&lt;br /&gt;3) This is perhaps one of my biggest gripes. It creates too much pressure on your eyeballs. Sure, you can adjust the tightness by messing with the velcro closure. But if you make it too loose, it will slip off your head. If you make it too tight, the mask will push against your eyes. Even if you keep it loose, the mask will still push against your eyes. I believe this is a design flaw of the mask. If you look where the velcro strips are, you will notice that it is in line with where your eyes would be. This causes the mask to crease at that point and put undue pressure on your eyes. Unlike cheaper masks that have pockets to prevent the mask from touching your eyes, this more expensive mask does not.&lt;br /&gt;4) It&#x27;s huge! This is a plus as well as a minus. It&#x27;s a plus because if the mask does slip a little, it will keep spears of light from getting through the edges. It&#x27;s a minus because no matter how you sleep, movement of your head will cause the mask to slip. There is no avoiding it. This mask will *NOT* stay where you put it. And most likely, when you wake up the next morning, you will probably not be wearing the mask anymore.&lt;br /&gt;4) I don&#x27;t get why this is patented. Is it because it claims to reduce noise? Puh-leze! Really? Is that little strip of cloth in some way supposed to block sound? I don&#x27;t feel that there is anything there other than the cloth material that is present in the rest of the sleep mask. It&#x27;s not as if there are sound deadeners embedded in the sleep mask...foam cups or something...nope...it&#x27;s just the cloth that extends over your ears..nothing more...there is nothing special about this...wrap a towel around your head and you will get a better sound deadener!&lt;br /&gt;5) That material that covers the ears, in fact *AMPLIFIES* noise! The material that covers the ears is part of the sleep mask as a whole! So if you lie on your stomach and the front of the mask brushes your pillow, this sound is transferred in an amplified manner to the material that covers your ears and is considerably louder than if it didn&#x27;t cover your ears at all. Same for if you sleep on your back. Any movement where the mask rubs against the pillow or blanket will transfer that noise in an amplified manner to your ears...It sounds like a record scratching it&#x27;s so loud!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What I did like about this thing is that it doesn&#x27;t skimp on material. My biggest problem with sleep masks is that it makes it extremely dark behind the mask. Then when you move, an edge may open up and a spear of light will stab through into this darkness and in your dark adjusted eyes, cause undue pain. This sleep mask is so large, that it if very difficult for it to move so extremely so that it will allow spears of light in. Unfortunately, because it is not opaque, you cannot get &amp;#34;cave darkness&amp;#34; inside the mask. There will always be a blue glow that you can clearly see with your eyes open or closed when wearing the mask.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This sleep mask makes a valiant attempt to solve a problem, but fails on all of them.&lt;br /&gt;What it would take to be the perfect sleep mask?&lt;br /&gt;1) eye cups. Keep the material off of my eyes&lt;br /&gt;2) use elastic for the straps&lt;br /&gt;3) allow the elastic to be adjustable not only for size but for where it is to be positioned on the actual sleep mask&lt;br /&gt;4) Put some kind of closed-cell foam in the cloth section that covers the ears&lt;br /&gt;5) make the material that covers the ears out of ultra suede of something similar that doesn&#x27;t transfer sound so easily.&lt;br /&gt;6) There is *NO* reason the stitching has to be on the edge of this thing...The stitching can be wrapped around and stitched to the front of the sleep mask. Yeah, it won&#x27;t look as pretty, but this is not a beauty pageant, we&#x27;re trying to get some sleep here!</li>

    <li> EDIT:  I&#x27;m keeping my original comments intact for those that initially have trouble as I did but see below for a correction.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Original review:&lt;br /&gt;------------------------&lt;br /&gt;I have had this eye mask on my Amazon Wishlist for what seems like forever and this past Christmas, my girlfriend finally got it for me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My initial impression was that it is the most comfortable eye mask i have ever used and the construction is top-notch.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then, after a few uses, I discovered it&#x27;s fatal flaw, which makes it ultimately unusable:  adjusting the mask snug enough so that it doesn&#x27;t move around or slip off my head during sleep causes the mask to apply a constant, gentle pressure directly on my eyes.  It&#x27;s not painful but after a full night&#x27;s sleep with the mask, I would wake up with blurred vision that would take between 1-3 hours to dissipate.  I experimented a few nights to determine if I was maybe doing something wrong but the issue is persistent or the mask is so loose it falls off.  I have an older eyemask with raised areas over the eye sockets and I even tried wearing that under this eye mask which seems to alleviate the issue but makes the mask more prone to slip out of place and is hotter, of course.  In the end, I decided it was more trouble than it&#x27;s worth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I emailed the manufacturer inquiring on this issue immediately after realizing what was happening and it&#x27;s been a few weeks and I have yet to hear back and frankly, don&#x27;t expect to at this point which makes for a poor service experience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have no idea if this issue could possibly cause permanent eye damage or reduced vision quality but I&#x27;m not risking it.  Which is a shame because as I stated before, it is the most comfortable eye mask I&#x27;ve ever used ... so comfortable, you don&#x27;t even notice it&#x27;s messing up your eyes.&lt;br /&gt;---------------------------&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EDIT:  After initially posting my review, the company reached out to me to acknowledge my concerns andprovided outstanding customer service, as well as being very apologetic that my initial contact to them through their website was not responded to in a timely fashion. They offered some wearing suggestions that I followed that corrected my issues.  I wish there had been a small slip of paper included with the mask that provided the proper wearing instructions or that it was posted on their website somewhere as I found the recommendations to be counter-intuitive.  With other typical masks I&#x27;ve used previously there are one or two elastic bands that go over or around your ears; even with two bands I&#x27;d typically wear both bands a bit high above the ears as to not have the elastic dig into the top of my ears while I slept and with ones that are adjustable I&#x27;d typically have them pretty snug as to not slip off during the night.  I&#x27;d never had similar issues with other masks but I prefer ones with raised cups over the eyes, it&#x27;s just a shame that most other masks are made of cheap material (especially the elastic they all seem to have that wears out in a matter of weeks).  As a matter of habit, I wore this sleep mask the same way as others: high and snug.  That is the wrong way to wear this mask.  The company suggested to me to wear with the back of the mask at the base of my skull and a bit loose.  Now, I had tried loosening the mask on my own as I mentioned above but even wearing directly over the ears, it would slip off.  Wearing it lower as recommended resolved the issues I was having with blurriness of my vision but felt weird at first until I adjusted to it. At the right size for my head to avoid the issue, it feels too loose but does not slip off or move around my head during the night. I&#x27;m still adjusting to it but I&#x27;m happy to report that the blurriness is (mostly) gone.  I&#x27;ve still had a couple of incidents with very minor blurriness but really only noticeable when I reading text on a computer screen (which is crucial for what I do for a living) and is now gonewithin a few minutes after waking up.  I&#x27;m assuming that with continued use I&#x27;ll acclimate to the mask better and that I&#x27;m still a bit hypercritical at this point having initially had such an alarming experience; those that don&#x27;t have to look at a computer screen or read a good bit of text first thing in the morning would likely never notice such an issue, so long as they are wearing the mask correctly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I highly urge the company to provide instructions with the masks or at least posted on their website going forward ... even if only a small handful of customers have similar issues such as myself, it&#x27;s a very jarring experience to have your eyesight affected.  As my initial review even stated, it&#x27;s an immensely comfortable mask and I&#x27;m delighted that now I can wear it.  The company is a small family owned business so I know it may not be feasible to start putting instructions in with their existing inventory but I hope to see something on their website at least and that they take my suggestion to heart for future production.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, I cannot emphasize enough that if my initial review or the handful of other similar negative reviews have put you off purchasing one, just do it.  Per the company&#x27;s website itself and the product description here, they do offer a 30 day money back guarantee so you have nothing to lose.  If you&#x27;ve used one before and were disappointed and had a similar experience as I did initially, take another look.</li>
